159

江蘇當江淮之衝濱海沮洄古稱澤國北納淮泗南鬱三江洪澤太湖苞孕千里水多陸

寡巨校頻仍往者無論矣民國十年以來水大三見元氣未復民鮮蓋藏今歲夏秋之間

奇雨崩騰逾月不止江淮湖海藹水橫流廬宅漂流禾苗盡沒死者枯棺蕩析生者屋脊

棲身一遇驚濤遂成魚鱉斯固天下之奇慘矣加以秋冬之際宿水不消種麥無期謀生 無躡賣兒鬻女露宿風餐奇慘之情尤難筆述此誠數百年未有之奇大也尤有陳者蘇

淞常鑷俱屬膏麒丟下諸河皆成樂土今則太湖漫淞江壅而四府皆夾洪湖溢三壩開 而裏河皆沒往歲一省偏夾不過數繇今則全省被大之縣五十有入實屬前古未聞節

經敝處派員分馳各屬逐地勘聳迅籌急抵前印一磊係屬初聳尙多遣

報前來詳細察覈討金陵道屬江寧句容淙水高淳江浦六合丹徒丹陽金壇溧

等縣滬海道屬南匯靑嬰奉賢金山川沙太倉嘉定寶山崇明海門等厤

常熟崑山吳江武進無錫宜興江陰蟒江南通如皋泰興等縣淮揚道屬淮陰淮安泗腸

漣水阜寧鹽城江都儀微東台興化泰縣高郵寶廌等謀徐海道屬銅山

碭山邳縣宿迆睢寧東海灌岑沐陽贛榆等縣均以大區大小夾民多寡列爲表冊

地圓以供衆莧惟是全省六十繇未被大者不過兩縣夾民多至九百餘萬人其 連之版有非鄭俠流民閻所能罄滔見者傷心聞者垂涙況江北大情尤重俗

江蘇省金陵道屬江甯縣調査災況簡明表

該螈西北滇江中貫淮河源流四達港汊紛歧全境田畝山圩各牛農民播種向以
災

受多毎遇風雨圩田先受其害本年自七月中旬以後霜雨颶風互作以致江潮暴漲河港漫 溢時當秩汎正盛無從疏洩低區悉成澤國圩堤圩梗經水激盪紛紛扇潰水深之處 通行其少數高原雖未波及然禾稻正在揚花吐穏亦因風雨諷搖梗仆花落被災之重
狀 況

歴年所未有「己由省撥款二千元先擇要散放急振」

圩等處為最重江東郷漼茱圩北固郷七里洲草鞋峽巴斗山等處大之

江蘇省金陵道屬高淳粿調査災尤簡明表
況狀災受

該縣地勢低下襟帶三湖全境圩田占十之七舊歴五月十九及二十一二三等日大雨如

注凹田禾稼已多受傷乃天不厭頑入秩後又復霜雨加以颶風山水漲發江潮項托以致 民大牛迤居高處搭藎草槐或移徙他方情形可憫

湖河飽脹低窪之區均已沖決漫沒田禾盡被傷損居民房屋多被水淹甚至坍塌被災各

堤圩決湞 I 莊村災被

各郷中小圩埠被淹者多不遑枚擧各大圩雖未潰決而圩內田禾亦多被淹

後

本年安徽水旱交校災情之重與災區之廣誠爲百餘年來所無茲撮載各方輯
＾中外士紳及輿論界之報告

一賑憮處蚌埠張坐辦之報告查皖北水災綠七入月間霈雨過多動輒經旬河流已覺

宣洩不及而淮河上游發源之河南榍柏縣蛟水下注至皖境霍邱縣三河尖入淮河幹流

淌河沙河瀨河澮河沱河淝河潼河英河淳河等水勢暴漲均入於淮氾濫漫溢周圍面積

千餘里一片汪洋不辨河流兼之入月中旬狂風暴雨六日不息雖堅如鐵路自固鑌至明

光獪沖壞數處斷絕交通所有太平阜陽潁上霍邱1 鳳 害 懷 達臺 五河 吁 眙天長，

纍城亳螈鳳碭宿縣靈璧定遠十入縣沖沒房屋田禾漂流人口牲畜不可勝數且有全莊

盡付洪流者所漲之水較尋常水平高至七入尺計皖境西自太阜東至泗盱長九百餘

下游江寐境內蓮湖水勢未消去路項託以致皖境水势僅落至尺餘依然一望無涯災民

之生存者流離失所餓李載道偶有高埠村莊縱或家有存糧而缺乏燃料亦不舉火詢之

4 來所未有至於皖中含山合肥無爲 高年人云此次水勢之大風力之猛積日之久爲百

巢縣和縣五縣被水沖破田圩愎寧宿松望江三縣先旱後澇皖南宣城當塗蕪湖繁晶四 綜計皖省被災縣分已過其牛矣

縣亦因破圩被淹萩浦東流兩縣夏秋之間久未得雨以上各縣被水受旱情形雖各不同

－李和溥調查阜潁之報告敬咯者竊和溥奉命調査皖北水災情形遙於九月十二日

與張公衡拱勉之趙淡邨諸君同時出發乘津浦快車至蚌埠十三日車過徐州卽略見水

過宿州至蚌埠水勢盆大車窗一望恍若舟行抵蚌留一日張公衡君在蚌接洽諸務溥等

十五日展輪上溯歷懷遠鳳壽霍潁阜等縣水勢浩漫日在照濡駭浪之中風湧波掀幾瀕

危險而環境呼號救命盆覺慘目傷心懐癖干地水深數丈城不沒者僅幾尺壽睬四門不

啓已三閱月矣鳳合城在山崗幸獲無恙而四郷則一片汪洋廬舍幾難蹤跡霍邱之澧河

放水素稱野渡該處居民無多牛以捕魚爲業餘地高崗尙多惟禾积亦深受風雨

患正陽水勢亦大十九H 至潁上縣知事以選舉赴阜次日輪舟朋抵阜賜城周圍民房倒

塌極多其順河街及附城之三里灣完全沖毀晤知事高潤之及當地慈善會諸人潁

利知事皆得接談聞阜陽以上水勢漸減河流將次順軌兩岸漸視阜以下潁以上河岸

已漸露惟溝塘湖堰漫溢充塞之區猶在在可観境內縱橫數百里尙有積潦深三四五六

尺不等二十一日由阜陽下駛抵阜潁交界之永興集和溥族居於是登岸但見屋宇絛圯

0 下趨尙可少免満積之患幸有一息尙存猶得聚 謀下 率 後 遊則衆流奔聚巨浸愈深若不

迷爲拯救則長此浩浩胥委沉淪是盆堪憫惻矣潁上視狀九區內惟一區之大

＇高未受水患而風雨摧殘收獲亦減其餘各區皆在阜之下逝而乂吡連毒鳳湖水

汪洋災情又當較重於阜也然自太和以下皆鮮完善之區沙河與淮河不祠淮河岸低一

遇大水卽若奇災今仆值此泛濫更凪浩劫沙河岸高而內身低窪此時岸已漸視惟是糊

場太廣不人其內不得其情若祗沿河一視面若無災因小敢避困難扁舟周歷冀狷其詳

聞阜腸當水勢緊急時有慈善會張澤普諸君紐－臨時救濟剧分六廁冒風雨乘舟攝賑

至受災最重處親手散放第六團由議員王宗詒敝族李子元李季英等出資數百元在永

然以中國政府狀朗為無力籌緤及此故被災各省長官有不得不遑請將非抵押

H

起霑雨經旬連宵逹H一或暫止片時旋仍滂沱如注以致平衍低窪各地水

深數尺某豆芝赧芋薯之凪沖洗無餘杭遣水浸風摧亦復瘍殘狼藉迨陰肜六月中旬始

露晴光猶冀水退後分栽某一旦菩麥以資補救詎下旬後鋂日恆有大雨風宙交作和高之

於入月十四五等日狂風大雨兩畫夜柿科偃仆水中稚斷穂落摧折殆盡於是＂回地同

奇災民房倒塌無算居民就岡阜支搭蔗棚苟延殘喘全境以濰溪古饒路町臨渙時村蘄

有澮淝沈澥諸水地臨淮河北岸西北地勢低窪易於受淹當七月初叫大雨兼旬上游徐

宿諸水狂奔下注窪地全遭淹沒濰河兩堰亦被沖決如楊畔禪啃木家湖麻湖澮塘溝尹

家集尤集各扇地勢極低所有莊村盡在水中溺無泮涯被災焓重其餘馮家阅＂回家集沙

灘比漁沭比朝北王，令盔陶山圩雙溝翎各處水亦甚深屮郷各界溝集婁莊北永定莊徐

元集常安集延干虻晏路日虞姬束竺桂山南郷濠城沱河束劉生西判集固鈕陸家梨張

家集各處被水没者淹害難粒被水深者秭頭微視南郷清河冏王家營高家老家陳家廟

吳家湖観音潘杜家橋楊家湖新梧呔家集後楊家簡家熵湯家湖九府集仁和比入逹扎

Any excessive amount of rain£ all would submerge the bays and the plains. Early in the sixth month of this summer, the heavy down-pour of rain lasting for weeks without ceasing, has made the water accumulate several feet in depth on the plain. Again, in addition to this, there is the water from Shan Hung and Ying Sha Rivers on the south-west, the flows from the Fei River on the west, the Hu How River and Cha Ho on the north-west, the streams of Shih Nie River . on the north and that from Chien River on the west, which combined together with Hwai River and the water from the lake created a landscape of shoreless water. Not only are the fall crops on the plain and the lowlund destroyed, but the maize on the hill-sides is also. As the rain fall has been so heavy and sudden and the water has risen so rapidly it is beyond our power to do any reclamation work at present. We may say that the heaviest calamity-strickened part in the region along the H wai and Fei Rivers next to this, is that in the north-eastern part. The fields which are submerged are about six-tenths of the whole area of the district. It is a great pity tCl see these people, both old and young, facing starvation, Shall we not do everything in our power to save them from total destruction?

6

Mr." Dodge, the Inspector at Pukow, told me that he had seen six dead· men on a raft. 1.'hese people had probably given up all hope of being saved and committed suicide by opening up their own arteries on the wrist. I went down on Monday last and returned here on Sunday evening, and I could not see that the water had gone down any in the flood region. People we met at railway stations told us that the loss of life must have been tremendous, as the floods came on very suddenly. All crops of course have entirely been destroyed and there is sure to be a lot of suffering in that region this winter. Unless something is done the water will remain where it is, as the land level is very low and there are no outlets. I have been told that if it had not been for the war the American Red Cross would have dug a new canal, which would have prevented this calamity to a great extent, had they been able to carry out their project. Several new lakes have been formed, covering_enormous tracts of country before cultivated, and these lakes having no outlet will remain there for years, as evaporation is the only way by which the water will be disposed- of, and unless some arrangements are made to assist the water in getting away it will stop there. Only a visit to the flooded region will give you an idea of the enormous tract of country that is under water. So far as I can learn, nothing at all was being done to collect the people stranded in the inundated region. I sincerely trust that you will be able to make some arrangements to help these unfortunate flood victims. Yours very sincerely, (Signed) T. A. RusTAD.

near Nansha11, in the .S函thern hills of Peng£ u, wherte it is sta國 many heartrending sights are to be seen. Although the water is already showiug signs of going down, the people are still unable to return to their homes, or the places where they used to be. It is stated that the famine which must follow this flood will be far more serious than the drought famine of the northern provinces of last year. The suffering in this province as well as others in close vicinity to it, all of which are clamouring for money to relieve the distress, promises another bard and trying winter for many mil1ions of Chinese. How it is possible for the government to go to their assistance in their present financial conditions it is impossible to see, and for that reason it is easy to understand why some of the provincial officials are requesti.t\g that they be allowed to retain some of the revenue, ,that is, those which are not ear-marked to meet or cover foreign obligations. Other provin 邙 s are trying to start lotteries, the profits of w.hich 、vill go to help to feed the starving.

Peking, September 14. The floods in Anhui province, according to private sources, are worse than they have been for the past hundred years. The heavy rains toward the end of summer which fell uninterruptedly for many days, caused the water of the Hwai river to suddenly rise, overflow its banks and break down the dykes. The water in a large number of places covers the land to a depth of ten feet. The thirt-een hsiens of Fuyang, Chunshang, Huochiu, Fengtai, Hwaiyuan, Mengcheng, Huoyang, Shuhsien, Lingpi, Ssuhsien, Wuho and Taiwu are all inundated and thousands of inhabitants are rendered homeless, their houses, property and crops having been swept ,away by the on-rushing water. The floods started at Kuchin-hsien in Honan, continuing to Fuyang and Huochi, th,:, s covering an ar.ea of some 30,000 :,quare Li. In a numbor of the inland district:, ,but a small percentage of the

445

`
contriving to remove the wat'er in hopes of replanting a late crop, there came heavy rains and big storms, lasting from the 16th to the 23rd of August. Before the water from the last rains had subsided this rain came, so that the inundated area was greatly enlarged and the land became a broad expanse of water. As the water was so high, and as there was no outlet for it, thousands of houses were submerged and in some places villages were completely under water. The sufferers are now either seen building mat sheds or are homeless and destitute, waiting for death. Of places which are partly elevated and partly low and so partly flooded are Sai T'ou P'oo, Chiai Kou Chi, Ta Hung Lin, K'ung T'ung, K'ung Kang, Ch'ang Chia Fen, Chang Foo, Li Hsin Chi, ^ Hsi Hsin Chi, Ho Lin, Lii Chia Ch'ien, Yu Ts'un, Ping O Sao, Shuang Miao, T'ang Chia Chi, Chu T'ung Ch'iao, Keng Chia Ts'un, Hu T'ung Chi, Sha Kiang Pa, Mou T'ang, Ch'ien Chia Han, Shih San, Hwai Shu Miao, Hung Ho Chi, Hung Chia Chi, Kao T'ang Tse, Loong T'ou Pa, and T'ang Chia Tien. The total area thus flooded is estimated at 26,000 mow (Chinese acres). Hwai Y1te1t:-Magistrate Li and Flood Inspector Pen presented a joint report, stating that at Hwai Yuen, which is at the junction of the streams of the H wai, K wo, Fei and Chien. there has been since the beginning of July heavy down-pours of rain so that all these streams have overflowed their banks, flooding all the fields and houses and turning the district into a vast expanse of water. The people old and young sought to build mat sheds beside hills or on more elevated ground for their temporary lodging. People even had to expose themselves in the open air both day and night. The homeless and destitute are indeed to be pitied! Places more remote from the streams ar,. rugged, hence difficult for travelling. It was only with much ado and much winding about that it was possible to reach all the places to make a thorough investigation. About two weeks ago, the magistrate went over all the different places and found that there were still some more elevated places that were not flooded. At present, the weather has been improving. The water has receded about one foot but cannot recede any more, because the Grand Canal has been filled up. How boundless the space of water seems! Those who are saved from flood, hav~ no houses to live in and will starve on the way. Although the village at Kao-poo has enough rice, y~t nothing cau be used as fuel for cooking. \Ve asked the old man about this- He told us that the destructiveness of the floods and of the winds and the length of time it has laste<l far exceeds what has been met with in these hundred years. The water has burst open the embankments at Hangshan, Ho-fei, Wu-wei, Chowhsi owhsien; in Hwaininghsien, Sou sung and \V ankiang the famine came first and then the flood; in Sen-tsen, Tangtu, Wuhu and Fan-chong the dikes are under water; and in Ch'iu-poo and Dong-liu there was no rain for the crops during summer and autumn. The number of afflicted districts exceeds half of the total number of districts in the whole of Anhwei Province. Foo Yang:-Magistrate Kau and Flood Inspector Lin presented a joint :report, stating that Foo Yang is all on a plain and that in the northeast there are the streams Yin, Yu, Fei, Tse, Chuen; in the southwest, Koo, Meng, Yen, Yuin, Ching; and besides, the district is along the course of the greater streams ·Hung and H wai. Every year when there is a · ·ttle too much rain, there is a flood, and when that is the case a tine crop is never to be expected. In the beginning of July this year, there was a great down-pour of rain both day and night and all the streams rose and overflowed at the same time, so that all the land along these streams was inundated. When the water receded, the people hastened to plant various kinds of grain; but who could have thought that in the beginning of August there would come another continual down-pour of rain for several days so that the streams would all rise and overflow again. The suffering due to floods in northern Anhwei this year is the greatest in a hundred years. Reports from the Chinese and Foreigners follow. I. Report of Mr. Chang, the Assistant of the Bureau of Flood Relief, Pengpu. The northern part of Anhwei Province suffered from flood on account of the swelling of great rivers due to long and continuous rains during July and August; the water filled up the river in the Tong-peh district which is the source of the Upper H wai Ho and it flows to the Ho Ch'iu district and Shan-ho-chien in Anhwei and therr enters into the H wai Ho; and the tributaries of the Hwai Ho一Wo Ho, Tasha Ho, Miao Ho, Kuei Ho, To Ho, Teh Ho, T'ong Ho, Hwang Ho, and Bah Ho, were suddenly all swollen t\P and their wafers all flowed to the H wai Ho. So it was overflowed, covering a large area over more than a thousand square Ii. Nothing could be seen there but waler and also the rivers could not be distinguished. Furthermore, the wind freshened into a gale and the rain fell for six days in succession in the middle of August. Even the railway from Koo-chen to Ming-kuan was broken by water in pl aces and communication was cut off.
